The Permissibility of Seeking Divine Openings
Al-Sawi refutes an objection about seeking divine openings through worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between seeking divine openings from God's grace and worshipping for the sake of obtaining those openings, and why the former is permissible while the latter is blameworthy.

Core Idea
Seeking God's bounty is commanded; worshipping for that bounty is not the way of the elite.

This passage addresses a subtle objection: if worship performed for a spiritual opening is considered a deterrent to sincerity, how can one be commanded to ask for such openings? Al-Sawi clarifies that requesting openings from God's grace is like asking for daily sustenance—it is a lawful request, not a transaction. The key is to distinguish between making supplication for God's favors and making those favors the motive of worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of the objection and the rebuttal.
2
Identify the objection's core
The objection claims that if worship for the sake of fath is a deterrent, then commanding to ask for fath is contradictory. Notice how Al-Sawi reframes the issue.
3
Understand the analogy
Al-Sawi compares seeking fath to asking for sustenance, health, and guidance. This shows that such requests are legitimate and even obligatory.
He cites the daily prayer for guidance.
4
Grasp the final distinction
The hashiyah emphasizes that the request (طلب) is not blameworthy, but worship (عبادة) for the sake of obtaining something is. Focus on this critical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يقال : إذا كانت العبادة من أجل الفتح من القواطع، فكيف يصحُ أن تأمره بطلبه بقولك : (وقل بذل ربِّ لا تقطعني عنك بقاطع). لأنَّا نقول : طلب الفتح من فيض فضل الله تعالى لا في مقابلة شيء لكن مع الاستقامة أمر مطلوب شرعاً كطلبك منه سعةَ الرّزق ، وصحة البدن والشّفاء من الأمراض الحسيَّة، ألا ترى أنَّه أوجب عليك طلب الهداية في كلِّ يوم وليلة سبعة عشرة مرَّة في قوله تعالى : اهْدِنَا الصِّرَاطَ الْمُسْتَقِيمَ ، وطلب منك ندباً غير ذلك في النوافل كثيراً بلا قوله : (لا يقال ... إلخ ) : عبَّر بذلك ؛ إشارة لضعف هذا التّوهُم وبعده . حد، وهذا غير العبادة لأجل حصول شيء؛ فإنَّها ليست طريقة المقربين، فافهم. قوله : (وهذا) : أي : الطلب المذكور. قوله :(فافهم) : أي : الفرق بين الطلب والعبادة، فطلب المراتب من الله تعالى غير مذموم والمذموم العبادة لذلك .
It should not be said: If worship for the sake of opening (fath) is among the deterrents (al-qawati'), then how can you command him to seek it by your saying: 'And say: O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter'? For we say: Seeking opening (fath) from the overflowing of the grace of God Almighty is not in exchange for anything, but with rectitude (al-istiqama) it is a matter required by the Law, like your asking Him for ample sustenance, health of the body, and recovery from physical illnesses. Do you not see that He obligated you to seek guidance every day and night seventeen times in His saying: 'Guide us to the straight path' (Quran 1:6), and He asked of you as a supererogatory act other than that in the supererogatory prayers many times without end. The comment on (it should not be said... etc.): He expressed this as an indication of the weakness of this illusion and its remoteness. 'End, and this is not worship for the sake of obtaining something; for it is not the way of the elite (al-muqarrabin), so understand. The comment on (and this): that is, the mentioned request. The comment on (so understand): that is, the difference between request and worship, for seeking ranks from God Almighty is not blameworthy, and what is blameworthy is worship for that.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The objection states that if worship performed for the sake of a spiritual opening (fath) is considered a deterrent to sincerity, then the poet's command to ask "O Lord, do not cut me off from You" would be contradictory. The answer clarifies that seeking openings from God's grace is not a transaction in exchange for worship; it is a permissible and even required request, like asking for daily sustenance or healing. The author supports this by noting that God commands the faithful to ask for guidance in every prayer. The goal is to distinguish the act of requesting blessings from worship that is motivated by the desire for those blessings. The hashiyah commentary reinforces that the objection is weak and that the real point is the distinction between seeking God's favors (which is commendable) and worshipping Him for the sake of those favors (which is blameworthy for the spiritual elite).

Key Terms
الفتح (fath)
القواطع (al-qawati')
الاستقامة (al-istiqama)
المقربين (al-muqarrabin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any request from God taints worship.
Correction: Seeking God's bounty is permissible and even commanded, as long as it does not become the motive for worship.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue about seeking divine openings (fath)?
A) It is forbidden because it spoils worship.
B) It is permissible and even commanded, but not as a motive for worship.
C) It is only for the prophets.
D) It is a form of worship itself.

Key Takeaway
Seeking divine openings from God's grace is permissible and even commanded, but worshipping for the sake of obtaining them is blameworthy for the elite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform your daily prayers, do you ever catch yourself thinking more about what you will get out of them (peace of mind, solution to a problem) than about simply standing before your Creator? What would it take to shift your intention to pure servitude, even for one prayer today?
?
The lesson distinguishes between asking Allah for blessings (permissible) and worshipping Him for the sake of obtaining blessings (blameworthy). Honestly examine your own worship: is there any act you do primarily because you want something from Allah? Are you willing to let go of that attachment and worship Him for His own sake, starting with your next obligatory prayer?
?
Consider the elite (al-muqarrabin) mentioned in this lesson. They do not worship for reward. Does that description match your current spiritual state? If not, what is the first step you can take today to purify your intention in one specific act of worship?

The Supplication for Divine Light and the Three Degrees of Certainty
The commentator explains the supplication for divine light and defines the three degrees of certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the supplication for divine light relates to the three degrees of certainty in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Certainty about truth comes in three degrees: proof, sight, and direct experience.

This passage from the commentary on al-Kharidat explains a supplication asking Allah for His 'secret'—the divine light that distinguishes truth from falsehood. The commentator then unpacks the adjective 'the most luminous' by describing three increasing degrees of certainty: knowledge by proof, knowledge by direct observation, and knowledge by direct experience. Understanding these levels helps us appreciate how the more immediate forms of knowledge bring deeper conviction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its flow. Then read the translation. Pay attention to how the commentator defines 'secret' and then moves to the three degrees.
2
Identify the three degrees of certainty
Find the terms علم اليقين, حق اليقين, and عين اليقين in the text. Note their definitions: knowledge by proof, by observation without mixing, and by mixing and merging.
3
Reflect on the fire analogy
The commentator uses the example of fire: inferring from smoke vs. seeing from a distance vs. being in the fire. Match each to one of the three degrees.
This helps internalize the hierarchy.
4
Connect the degrees to the supplication
The supplication asks for the 'secret' which is the most luminous light. Which degree of certainty does that correspond to? How does this shape your understanding of the prayer?
The highest degree is عين اليقين.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) قل بذل : يا رب لا تحرمني) - بفتح التاء - من حرم، أو (لا بضمها من أحرم، بمعنى منع ; أي لا تمنعني (من) إعطاء (سرك)، المراد به : النُّور الإلهي الذي يفرِّق به العبد بين الحق والباطل في نفس الأمر المشار إليه بقوله تعالى : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِن تَتَّقُوا اللَّهَ يَجْعَل لَكُمْ فُرْقَانًا ) (۱) ; أي نوراً في قلوبكم تميزون به بين الحق والباطل على ما هو عليه في نفس الأمر. (الأبهى) أي : الأنور من كلّ نور، فإنَّ علم اليقين – وهو معرفة الأشياء بالبرهان - نور، وأنور منه حقُّ اليقين – وهو معرفتها بالمشاهدة من غير مخالطة وممازجة - وأنور منه عين اليقين – وهو معرفتها بالمخالطة والممازجة، فليس من استدل على وجود نار برؤية الدُّخان كمن شاهدها على بُعد وليس من شاهدها كمن خالطها وعلم وقودها وما هي عليه .
And say: 'O Lord, do not deprive me' - with fatha on the ta - from harama, or (with damma from ahrama, meaning to prevent; i.e., do not prevent me from giving (Your secret), intended by it: the divine light by which the servant distinguishes between truth and falsehood in themselves, indicated by His saying: 'O you who have believed, if you fear Allah, He will grant you a criterion' (Quran 8:29); i.e., a light in your hearts by which you distinguish between truth and falsehood as it is in itself. (The more luminous) i.e., the most luminous of every light, for knowledge of certainty - which is knowledge of things by proof - is light, and more luminous than it is the truth of certainty - which is knowledge of things by direct observation without mixing and merging - and more luminous than it is the eye of certainty - which is knowledge of things by mixing and merging. So the one who infers the existence of fire by seeing smoke is not like the one who sees it from a distance, nor is the one who sees it like the one who mixes with it and knows its fuel and its state.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line of supplication from the original poem. The commentator first explains the phrase 'do not deprive me of Your secret' (سرك), where 'secret' is defined as the divine light (النور الإلهي) by which a servant distinguishes truth from falsehood. He supports this with Quran 8:29, which speaks of a 'criterion' (فرقان) as a light in the hearts. Then he explains the adjective 'الأبهى' (the most luminous) by describing three degrees of certainty: علم اليقين (knowledge of certainty) obtained through proof (برهان), حق اليقين (truth of certainty) obtained by direct observation without mixing (مشاهدة), and عين اليقين (eye of certainty) obtained by direct experience with mixing and merging (مخالطة وممازجة). He illustrates with an example of fire: someone inferring fire from smoke (علم اليقين) is less direct than someone seeing fire from a distance (حق اليقين), and seeing from a distance is less direct than actually being in the fire and experiencing it (عين اليقين). This shows the hierarchy of knowledge.

Key Terms
سر
نور إلهي
فرقان
علم اليقين
عين اليقين
حق اليقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking the three levels are separate types of knowledge rather than degrees of strength and directness of certainty.
Correction: The passage presents them as a hierarchy: each level is more luminous and immediate than the previous, culminating in direct experience.

Checkpoint
Which of the three levels of certainty is described as knowledge obtained by proof (برهان)?
A) عين اليقين
B) حق اليقين
C) علم اليقين
D) جميع ما ذكر

Key Takeaway
The supplication seeks direct experience of divine light, which represents the highest degree of certainty (عين اليقين).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek certainty about a religious truth, do you settle for intellectual proof (ilm al-yaqin) or do you yearn for direct experience that transforms your heart? Which level are you truly living at right now?
?
The fire analogy shows that being told about fire is not enough—you must be in it. What 'fire' of truth are you avoiding experiencing directly? What holds you back from mixing with it?
?
If divine light distinguishes truth from falsehood in your heart, why do you still cling to falsehood? Ask yourself: am I willing to suffer the pain of direct experience to gain that light?

Quranic Proofs for the Three Levels of Certainty
Commentator provides Quranic verses as evidence for each of the three levels of certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran provides distinct verses for each of the three levels of certainty: knowledge of certainty, eye of certainty, and truth of certainty.

Core Idea
Each level of certainty has a specific Quranic verse that perfectly matches its nature.

The commentator now grounds the abstract threefold classification of certainty in direct Quranic evidence. He shows that these are not merely logical categories but are rooted in revelation itself. Let's see how each verse corresponds to its respective level of certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the structure: a summary statement, then three verses each introduced clearly.
2
Identify each level and its verse
Match each level (علم اليقين, عين اليقين, حق اليقين) to the verse the commentator cites. See how the wording of each verse mirrors the level's name.
The first verse mentions 'knowledge', the second 'eye', the third 'truth'.
3
Understand the balanced arrangement
The commentator notes that the fire example earlier in the text is a 'laf wa nashr murattab' – a balanced arrangement where the examples correspond in order to the levels.
This shows the author's deliberate ordering.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider that these verses are not random; each is chosen because its wording matches the nature of that level of certainty.
This deepens your appreciation for the Quran's precision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإنَّ علم اليقين ... إلخ) حاصل ما ذكره أنَّ الأمور ثلاثة : علم يقين، وعين يقين، وحق يقين، وكلُّها مذكورة في القرآن، أمَّا الأول : فقال الله فيه : لَوْ تَعْلَمُونَ عِلْمَ الْيَقِينِ لَتَرُونَ الْجَحِيمَ ) (٢ ) . والثَّاني : قال الله فيه : ثُمَّ لَتَرَوْنَهَا عَيْنَ الْيَقِينِ (1) . والثَّالث : قال الله فيه : فَنُزُلٌ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَتَصْلِيَةُ جَحِيمٍ إِنَّ هَذَا هُوَ حَقُّ الْيَقِينِ (٢) . قوله : ( فليس من استدل على وجود نار . . . إلخ) : لف ونشر مرتب .
His statement: ('For knowledge of certainty... etc.') The summary of what he mentioned is that matters are three: knowledge of certainty, eye of certainty, and truth of certainty, and all are mentioned in the Quran. As for the first: Allah said concerning it: 'If you knew with certainty of knowledge, you would see the Hellfire' (Quran 102:5-6). And the second: Allah said concerning it: 'Then you shall surely see it with the eye of certainty' (Quran 102:7). And the third: Allah said concerning it: 'A hospitality of boiling water and a burning of Hellfire; indeed, this is the truth of certainty' (Quran 56:93-95). His statement: ('So the one who infers the existence of fire... etc.') is a balanced arrangement (laf wa nashr murattab).
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is a gloss on the earlier explanation of the three levels of certainty. The commentator summarizes that the author (of the original poem) mentioned three types of certainty: علم اليقين, عين اليقين, and حق اليقين, and then provides a Quranic verse for each. For علم اليقين, he cites Quran 102:5-6, which speaks of seeing Hellfire if one had knowledge of certainty. For عين اليقين, he cites Quran 102:7, which says 'then you shall surely see it with the eye of certainty'. For حق اليقين, he cites Quran 56:93-95, which describes the punishment as 'the truth of certainty'. The commentator then notes that the fire example earlier in the text is a 'laf wa nashr murattab' (balanced arrangement), meaning that the three examples correspond in order to the three levels.

عين اليقين
حق اليقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verses are random examples, not specifically chosen for each level.
Correction: Each verse is precisely matched: the first mentions 'knowledge', the second 'eye', the third 'truth', showing deliberate precision.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The three levels of certainty are not just logical constructs; they are confirmed by specific Quranic verses that echo their names.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that if you had 'knowledge of certainty', you would see the Hellfire. Do you actually live with that knowledge? When was the last time your awareness of Hellfire changed a small decision you made today?
?
The verse says you will see the Hellfire with the 'eye of certainty'. Imagine standing before it. Right now, what in your life would you regret not leaving behind? Write one specific thing you will do today to ensure that regret does not materialize.
?
The punishment of Hellfire is called 'the truth of certainty'. Do you treat that truth as more real than the phone in your hand? If not, what is one concrete step you can take this week to let that truth shape your daily routine?

The Three Levels of Yaqin and the Benefit of Du'a
Al-Sawi explains the three levels of yaqin and affirms the benefit of du'a against the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three degrees of certainty ('ilm al-yaqin, 'ayn al-yaqin, haqq al-yaqin) and how they affirm the benefit of supplication (du'a) against the objection of the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Certainty has degrees; du'a is beneficial and part of divine decree.

In this passage, Al-Sawi unpacks the three levels of certainty with the classic fire example, and then draws an important practical conclusion: that du'a (supplication) is indeed beneficial, contrary to the Mu'tazila who argue it is futile against predetermined decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three levels of yaqin
Find the three names of certainty: 'ilm al-yaqin, 'ayn al-yaqin, haqq al-yaqin. Note how each is defined differently.
The fire analogy illustrates the progression.
3
Analyze the fire analogy
Understand the example: inferring fire from smoke is not like seeing it, and seeing it is not like experiencing it directly.
This analogy shows the hierarchy of knowledge.
4
Note the indication that du'a benefits
Al-Sawi says the author's words indicate du'a is beneficial. Look for the phrase that indicates this and the evidence from Quran and Sunna.
5
Understand the Mu'tazila position and the response
The Mu'tazila argue that du'a is unnecessary because decree is fixed. Al-Sawi refutes this by showing du'a is itself decreed and beneficial.
This is a key theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالمشاهدة من غير مخالطة وممازجة - وأنور منه عين اليقين – وهو معرفتها بالمخالطة والممازجة، فليس من استدل على وجود نار برؤية الدُّخان كمن شاهدها على بُعد وليس من شاهدها كمن خالطها وعلم وقودها وما هي عليه . (المزيل للعمى) يعني : الجهل، وفي كلامه إشارة إلى أنَّ الدُّعاء ينفع، وهو ممَّا لا شكّ فيه عند أهل الحقِّ، والقرآن العظيم مشحون به، وهو في السُّنَّة أكثر من أن يُحصى، خلافاً للمعتزلة ويجب والثَّاني : قال الله فيه : ثُمَّ لَتَرَوْنَهَا عَيْنَ الْيَقِينِ (1) ٩٤ ألا والثَّالث : قال الله فيه : فَتَرُلٌ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَنَصْلِهُ جَمِيمٍ إِنَّ هَذَا هُوَ (۲) حَقُّ الْيَقِينِ (٢) . ۹۳ قوله : ( فليس من استدل على وجود نار . . . إلخ) : لف ونشر مرتب . قوله : (يعني: الجهل: أشار بذلك إلى أنَّ المراد بالعمى المعنوي؛ وهو انطماس البصيرة. قوله : (إلى أنَّ الدعاء ينفع) : أي : ممَّا نزل ومما لم ينزل . قوله : ( عند أهل الحقِّ أي وهم أهل السنة والجماعة. قوله : (خلافاً للمعتزلة) : أي : حيث قالوا بعدم جواز الدُّعاء؛ محتجين بأنَّ ما قدَّره الله يكون فلا حاجة للدُّعاء، ويفسرون الدُّعاء المذكور في
By observation without mixing and intermingling – and more luminous than it is 'ayn al-yaqin (the eye of certainty) – which is knowing it by mixing and intermingling. So the one who infers the existence of fire by seeing smoke is not like the one who witnesses it from afar, and the one who witnesses it is not like the one who mixes with it and knows its fuel and what it is. (The remover of blindness) means ignorance. And in his statement is an indication that supplication (du'a) is beneficial, and it is something about which there is no doubt among the people of truth, and the great Qur'an is filled with it, and it is in the Sunna beyond enumeration, contrary to the Mu'tazila. And it is necessary. And the second: Allah said concerning it: 'Then you will surely see it with the eye of certainty' (7). And the third: Allah said concerning it: 'Then you will drink of boiling water, and drink of a boiling hot spring, indeed this is the truth of certainty' (93-95). His statement: (So the one who infers the existence of fire... etc.) is an orderly redistribution and arrangement. His statement: (meaning: ignorance) he indicated by that that what is meant by blindness is spiritual blindness, which is the blunting of insight. His statement: (that supplication benefits) i.e., for what has descended and what has not descended. His statement: (according to the people of truth) i.e., they are Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. His statement: (contrary to the Mu'tazila) i.e., they said that supplication is not permissible, arguing that what Allah has decreed will be, so there is no need for supplication, and they interpret the supplication mentioned in the verses as worship.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage defines the three levels of yaqin (certainty) and uses them to affirm the benefit of du'a (supplication) against the Mu'tazila. It begins by distinguishing three modes of knowing something: mere observation from a distance ('ilm al-yaqin), direct sight ('ayn al-yaqin), and intimate experience (haqq al-yaqin). The example of fire illustrates this: inferring fire from smoke is not like seeing it from afar, and seeing it is not like mixing with it and knowing its fuel. The commentator then explains that the phrase 'al-muzil li-l-'ama' (the remover of blindness) refers to ignorance (jahl), i.e., spiritual blindness. The author's statement indicates that du'a is beneficial, a point on which there is no doubt among Ahl al-Haqq (i.e., Ahl al-Sunna), and the Qur'an and Sunna are filled with it. This is contrary to the Mu'tazila, who deny the benefit of du'a, arguing that whatever Allah has decreed will happen regardless. They interpret the du'a mentioned in the Qur'an as merely worship, not a means of altering decree. The passage then cites two Qur'anic verses to illustrate the higher levels of yaqin. The commentator clarifies that the example of fire is a well-ordered analogy (laf wa nashr murattab). He also explains that the du'a benefits both for what has been decreed and what has not, and notes that Ahl al-Sunna are the people of truth.

Key Terms
يقين
دعاء
معتزلة
علم اليقين
عين اليقين
حق اليقين
العمى المعنوي
أهل الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Du'a cannot change what Allah has decreed, so it is useless.
Correction: Du'a is itself decreed by Allah and is a means by which His decree is realized; therefore it is beneficial.

Checkpoint
What is the primary argument of the Mu'tazila against the benefit of du'a according to this passage?
A) Du'a is never answered.
B) Whatever Allah has decreed will happen, so du'a is unnecessary.
C) Du'a is only for worship, not for requesting needs.
D) Du'a is permissible only in times of distress.

Key Takeaway
The three levels of certainty illustrate the depth of knowledge, and du'a is an integral part of divine decree, not an attempt to change it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Where does your certainty about Allah and His decrees currently stand—are you content with mere inference from signs, or have you sought direct experience through sincere worship and reliance on Him? What step will you take today to deepen your yaqin?
?
When you make du'a, do you struggle with the feeling that it might be useless against what is already written? Will you commit to seeing du'a as part of Allah's decree—a cause He has gifted you to change outcomes—and offer it with full conviction starting tonight?
?
This passage depicts the spiritual blindness of ignorance. Look honestly at your own life: in what areas have you been spiritually blind, relying on assumptions rather than seeking the light of direct knowledge? What is one habit or belief you must confront immediately to remove that blindness?
